err != nil {\n   330→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attaching cilium_host: %w\", err)\n   331→\t}\n   332→\n   333→\treturn nil\n   334→}\n   335→\n   336→// attachCiliumHost inserts the host endpoint's policy program into the global\n   337→// cilium_call_policy map and attaches programs from bpf_host.c to cilium_host.\n   338→func attachCiliumHost(ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n   339→\thost, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(ep.InterfaceName())\n   340→\tif err != nil {\n   341→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"retrieving device %s: %w\", ep.InterfaceName(), err)\n   342→\t}\n   343→\n   344→\tvar hostObj hostObjects\n   345→\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&hostObj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n   346→\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n   347→\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n   348→\t\t},\n   349→\t\tMapRenames: ELFMapSubstitutions(ep),\n   350→\t\tConstants:  ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep),\n   351→\t})\n   352→\tif err != nil {\n   353→\t\treturn err\n   354→\t}\n   355→\tdefer hostObj.Close()\n   356→\n   357→\t// Insert host endpoint policy program.\n   358→\tif err := hostObj.PolicyMap.Update(uint32(ep.GetID()), hostObj.PolicyProg, ebpf.UpdateAny); err != nil {\n   359→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"inserting host endpoint policy program: %w\", err)\n   360→\t}\n   361→\n   362→\t// Attach cil_to_host to cilium_host ingress.\n   363→\tif err := attachSKBProgram(host, hostObj.ToHost, symbolToHostEp,\n   364→\t\tbpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), host), netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   365→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s ingress: %w\", ep.InterfaceName(), err)\n   366→\t}\n   367→\t// Attach cil_from_host to cilium_host egress.\n   368→\tif err := attachSKBProgram(host, hostObj.FromHost, symbolFromHostEp,\n   369→\t\tbpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), host), netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   370→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s egress: %w\", ep.InterfaceName(), err)\n   371→\t}\n   372→\n   373→\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n   374→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n   375→\t}\n   376→\n   377→\treturn nil\n   378→}\n   379→\n   380→// attachCiliumNet attaches programs from bpf_host.c to cilium_net.\n   381→func attachCiliumNet(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n   382→\tnet, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(defaults.SecondHostDevice)\n   383→\tif err != nil {\n   384→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"retrieving device %s: %w\", defaults.SecondHostDevice, err)\n   385→\t}\n   386→\n   387→\tconsts, renames, err := hostRewrites(cfg, ep, defaults.SecondHostDevice)\n   388→\tif err != nil {\n   389→\t\treturn err\n   390→\t}\n   391→\n   392→\tvar netObj hostNetObjects\n   393→\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&netObj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n   394→\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n   395→\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n   396→\t\t},\n   397→\t\tMapRenames: renames,\n   398→\t\tConstants:  consts,\n   399→\t})\n   400→\tif err != nil {\n   401→\t\treturn err\n   402→\t}\n   403→\tdefer netObj.Close()\n   404→\n   405→\t// Attach cil_to_host to cilium_net.\n   406→\tif err := attachSKBProgram(net, netObj.ToHost, symbolToHostEp,\n   407→\t\tbpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), net), netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   408→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s ingress: %w\", defaults.SecondHostDevice, err)\n   409→\t}\n   410→\n   411→\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n   412→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n   413→\t}\n   414→\n   415→\treturn nil\n   416→}\n   417→\n   418→// attachNetworkDevices attaches programs from bpf_host.c to externally-facing\n   419→// devices and the wireguard device. Attaches cil_from_netdev to ingress and\n   420→// optionally cil_to_netdev to egress if enabled features require it.\n   421→func attachNetworkDevices(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n   422→\tdevices := cfg.DeviceNames()\n   423→\n   424→\t// Selectively attach bpf_host to cilium_wg0.\n   425→\tif option.Config.NeedBPFHostOnWireGuardDevice() {\n   426→\t\tdevices = append(devices, wgTypes.IfaceName)\n   427→\t}\n   428→\n   429→\t// Replace programs on physical devices, ignoring devices that don't exist.\n   430→\tfor _, device := range devices {\n   431→\t\tiface, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(device)\n   432→\t\tif err != nil {\n   433→\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).WithField(\"device\", device).Warn(\"Link does not exist\")\n   434→\t\t\tcontinue\n   435→\t\t}\n   436→\n   437→\t\tlinkDir := bpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), iface)\n   438→\n   439→\t\tconsts, renames, err := hostRewrites(cfg, ep, device)\n   440→\t\tif err != nil {\n   441→\t\t\treturn err\n   442→\t\t}\n   443→\n   444→\t\tvar netdevObj hostNetdevObjects\n   445→\t\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&netdevObj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n   446→\t\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n   447→\t\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n   448→\t\t\t},\n   449→\t\t\tMapRenames: renames,\n   450→\t\t\tConstants:  consts,\n   451→\t\t})\n   452→\t\tif err != nil {\n   453→\t\t\treturn err\n   454→\t\t}\n   455→\t\tdefer netdevObj.Close()\n   456→\n   457→\t\t// Attach cil_from_netdev to ingress.\n   458→\t\tif err := attachSKBProgram(iface, netdevObj.FromNetdev, symbolFromHostNetdevEp,\n   459→\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   460→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s ingress: %w\", device, err)\n   461→\t\t}\n   462→\n   463→\t\t// When downgrading from v1.18, upon successfully attaching cil_from_netdev\n   464→\t\t// to cilium_wg0, we must remove the cil_from_wireguard program.\n   465→\t\tif device == wgTypes.IfaceName {\n   466→\t\t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(iface, symbolFromWireguard,\n   467→\t\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS); err != nil {\n   468→\t\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n   469→\t\t\t}\n   470→\t\t\t// Cleanup also calls map from v1.18 after downgrade.\n   471→\t\t\tcleanCallsMaps(fmt.Sprintf(\"cilium_calls_wireguard_%d\", iface.Attrs().Index))\n   472→\t\t}\n   473→\n   474→\t\tif option.Config.AreDevicesRequired() {\n   475→\t\t\t// Attaching bpf_host to cilium_wg0 is required for encrypting KPR\n   476→\t\t\t// traffic. Only ingress prog (aka \"from-netdev\") is needed to handle\n   477→\t\t\t// the rev-NAT xlations.\n   478→\t\t\tif device != wgTypes.IfaceName {\n   479→\t\t\t\t// Attach cil_to_netdev to egress.\n   480→\t\t\t\tif err := attachSKBProgram(iface, netdevObj.ToNetdev, symbolToHostNetdevEp,\n   481→\t\t\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   482→\t\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s egress: %w\", device, err)\n   483→\t\t\t\t}\n   484→\t\t\t}\n   485→\t\t} else {\n   486→\t\t\t// Remove any previously attached device from egress path if BPF\n   487→\t\t\t// NodePort and host firewall are disabled.\n   488→\t\t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(iface, symbolToHostNetdevEp, linkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS); err != nil {\n   489→\t\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n   490→\t\t\t}\n   491→\t\t}\n   492→\n   493→\t\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n   494→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n   495→\t\t}\n   496→\t}\n   497→\n   498→\t// Call immediately after attaching programs to make it obvious that a\n   499→\t// program was wrongfully detached due to a bug or misconfiguration.\n   500→\tif err := removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms(devices); err != nil {\n   501→\t\tlog.WithError(err).Error(\"Failed to remove obsolete netdev programs\")\n   502→\t}\n   503→\n   504→\treturn nil\n   505→}\n   506→\n   507→// reloadEndpoint loads programs in spec into the device used by ep.\n   508→//\n   509→// spec is modified by the method and it is the callers responsibility to copy\n   510→// it if necessary.\n   511→func reloadEndpoint(ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n   512→\tdevice := ep.InterfaceName()\n   513→\n   514→\tvar obj lxcObjects\n   515→\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&obj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n   516→\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n   517→\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n   518→\t\t},\n   519→\t\tMapRenames: ELFMapSubstitutions(ep),\n   520→\t\tConstants:  ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep),\n   521→\t})\n   522→\tif err != nil {\n   523→\t\treturn err\n   524→\t}\n   525→\tdefer obj.Close()\n   526→\n   527→\t// Insert policy programs before attaching entrypoints to tc hooks.\n   528→\t// Inserting a policy program is considered an attachment, since it makes\n   529→\t// the code reachable by bpf_host when it evaluates policy for the endpoint.\n   530→\t// All internal tail call plumbing needs to be done before this point.\n   531→\t// If the agent dies uncleanly after the first program has been inserted,\n   532→\t// the endpoint's connectivity will be partially broken or exhibit undefined\n   533→\t// behaviour like missed tail calls or drops.\n   534→\tif err := obj.PolicyMap.Update(uint32(ep.GetID()), obj.PolicyProg, ebpf.UpdateAny); err != nil {\n   535→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"inserting endpoint policy program: %w\", err)\n   536→\t}\n   537→\tif err := obj.EgressPolicyMap.Update(uint32(ep.GetID()), obj.EgressPolicyProg, ebpf.UpdateAny); err != nil {\n   538→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"inserting endpoint egress policy program: %w\", err)\n   539→\t}\n   540→\n   541→\tiface, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(device)\n   542→\tif err != nil {\n   543→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"retrieving device %s: %w\", device, err)\n   544→\t}\n   545→\n   546→\tlinkDir := bpffsEndpointLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), ep)\n   547→\tif err := attachSKBProgram(iface, obj.FromContainer, symbolFromEndpoint,\n   548→\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   549→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s ingress: %w\", device, err)\n   550→\t}\n   551→\n   552→\tif ep.RequireEgressProg() {\n   553→\t\tif err := attachSKBProgram(iface, obj.ToContainer, symbolToEndpoint,\n   554→\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   555→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s egress: %w\", device, err)\n   556→\t\t}\n   557→\t} else {\n   558→\t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(iface, symbolToEndpoint, linkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS); err != nil {\n   559→\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n   560→\t\t}\n   561→\t}\n   562→\n   563→\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n   564→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n   565→\t}\n   566→\n   567→\tif ep.RequireEndpointRoute() {\n   568→\t\tscopedLog := ep.Logger(subsystem).WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n   569→\t\t\tlogfields.Interface: device,\n   570→\t\t})\n   571→\t\tif ip := ep.IPv4Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n   572→\t\t\tif err := upsertEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip)); err != nil {\n   573→\t\t\t\tscopedLog.WithError(err).Warn(\"Failed to upsert route\")\n   574→\t\t\t}\n   575→\t\t}\n   576→\t\tif ip := ep.IPv6Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n   577→\t\t\tif err := upsertEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip)); err != nil {\n   578→\t\t\t\tscopedLog.WithError(err).Warn(\"Failed to upsert route\")\n   579→\t\t\t}\n   580→\t\t}\n   581→\t}\n   582→\n   583→\treturn nil\n   584→}\n   585→\n   586→func replaceOverlayDatapath(ctx context.Context, cArgs []string, device netlink.Link) error {\n   587→\tif err := compileOverlay(ctx, cArgs); err != nil {\n   588→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"compiling overlay program: %w\", err)\n   589→\t}\n   590→\n   591→\tspec, err := bpf.LoadCollectionSpec(overlayObj)\n   592→\tif err != nil {\n   593→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"loading eBPF ELF %s: %w\", overlayObj, err)\n   594→\t}\n   595→\n   596→\tvar obj overlayObjects\n   597→\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&obj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n   598→\t\tConstants: map[string]uint64{\n   599→\t\t\t\"interface_ifindex\": uint64(device.Attrs().Index),\n   600→\t\t},\n   601→\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n   602→\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n   603→\t\t},\n   604→\t})\n   605→\tif err != nil {\n   606→\t\treturn err\n   607→\t}\n   608→\tdefer obj.Close()\n   609→\n   610→\tlinkDir := bpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), device)\n   611→\tif err := attachSKBProgram(device, obj.FromOverlay, symbolFromOverlay,\n   612→\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   613→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s ingress: %w\", device, err)\n   614→\t}\n   615→\tif err := attachSKBProgram(device, obj.ToOverlay, symbolToOverlay,\n   616→\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   617→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s egress: %w\", device, err)\n   618→\t}\n   619→\n   620→\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n   621→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n   622→\t}\n   623→\n   624→\treturn nil\n   625→}\n   626→\n   627→func replaceWireguardDatapath(ctx context.Context, cArgs []string, device netlink.Link) (err error) {\n   628→\tif err := compileWireguard(ctx, cArgs); err != nil {\n   629→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"compiling wireguard program: %w\", err)\n   630→\t}\n   631→\n   632→\tspec, err := bpf.LoadCollectionSpec(wireguardObj)\n   633→\tif err != nil {\n   634→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"loading eBPF ELF %s: %w\", wireguardObj, err)\n   635→\t}\n   636→\n   637→\tvar obj wireguardObjects\n   638→\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&obj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n   639→\t\tConstants: map[string]uint64{\n   640→\t\t\t\"interface_ifindex\": uint64(device.Attrs().Index),\n   641→\t\t},\n   642→\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n   643→\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n   644→\t\t},\n   645→\t})\n   646→\tif err != nil {\n   647→\t\treturn err\n   648→\t}\n   649→\tdefer obj.Close()\n   650→\n   651→\tlinkDir := bpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), device)\n   652→\t// Attach/detach cil_to_wireguard to/from egress.\n   653→\tif option.Config.NeedEgressOnWireGuardDevice() {\n   654→\t\tif err := attachSKBProgram(device, obj.ToWireguard, symbolToWireguard,\n   655→\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n   656→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s egress: %w\", device, err)\n   657→\t\t}\n   658→\t} else {\n   659→\t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(device, symbolToWireguard,\n   660→\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS); err != nil {\n   661→\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n   662→\t\t}\n   663→\t}\n   664→\t// Selectively detach cil_from_netdev from ingress.\n   665→\tif !option.Config.NeedBPFHostOnWireGuardDevice() {\n   666→\t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(device, symbolFromHostNetdevEp,\n   667→\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS); err != nil {\n   668→\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", wgTypes.IfaceName).Error(err)\n   669→\t\t}\n   670→\t\t// When downgrading from v1.18 we must also detach cil_from_wireguard:\n   671→\t\t// - if the hook is still needed, then cil_from_wireguard is removed in\n   672→\t\t//   attachNetworkDevices() as soon as cil_from_netdev is inserted;\n   673→\t\t// - otherwise we handle here its removal.\n   674→\t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(device, symbolFromWireguard,\n   675→\t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS); err != nil {\n   676→\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n   677→\t\t}\n   678→\t\t// Cleanup also calls map from v1.18 after downgrade.\n   679→\t\tcleanCallsMaps(fmt.Sprintf(\"cilium_calls_wireguard_%d\", device.Attrs().Index))\n   680→\t}\n   681→\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n   682→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n   683→\t}\n   684→\treturn nil\n   685→}\n   686→\n   687→// ReloadDatapath reloads the BPF datapath programs for the specified endpoint.\n   688→//\n   689→// It attempts to find a pre-compiled\n   690→// template datapath object to use, to avoid a costly compile operation.\n   691→// Only if there is no existing template that has the same configuration\n   692→// parameters as the specified endpoint, this function will compile a new\n   693→// template for this configuration.\n   694→//\n   695→// This function will block if the cache does not contain an entry for the\n   696→// same EndpointConfiguration and multiple goroutines attempt to concurrently\n   697→// CompileOrLoad with the same configuration parameters. When the first\n   698→// goroutine completes compilation of the template, all other CompileOrLoad\n   699→// invocations will be released.\n   700→func (l *loader) ReloadDatapath(ctx context.Context, ep datapath.Endpoint, cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, stats *metrics.SpanStat) (string, error) {\n   701→\tdirs := directoryInfo{\n   702→\t\tLibrary: option.Config.BpfDir,\n   703→\t\tRuntime: option.Config.StateDir,\n   704→\t\tState:   ep.StateDir(),\n   705→\t\tOutput:  ep.StateDir(),\n   706→\t}\n   707→\n   708→\tspec, hash, err := l.templateCache.fetchOrCompile(ctx, cfg, ep, &dirs, stats)\n   709→\tif err != nil {\n   710→\t\treturn \"\", err\n   711→\t}\n   712→\n   713→\tif ep.IsHost() {\n   714→\t\t// Reload bpf programs on cilium_host and cilium_net.\n   715→\t\tstats.BpfLoadProg.Start()\n   716→\t\terr = reloadHostEndpoint(cfg, ep, spec)\n   717→\t\tstats.BpfLoadProg.End(err == nil)\n   718→\n   719→\t\tl.hostDpInitializedOnce.Do(func() {\n   720→\t\t\tlog.Debug(\"Initialized host datapath\")\n   721→\t\t\tclose(l.hostDpInitialized)\n   722→\t\t})\n   723→\n   724→\t\treturn hash, err\n   725→\t}\n   726→\n   727→\t// Reload an lxc endpoint program.\n   728→\tstats.BpfLoadProg.Start()\n   729→\terr = reloadEndpoint(ep, spec)\n   730→\tstats.BpfLoadProg.End(err == nil)\n   731→\treturn hash, err\n   732→}\n   733→\n   734→// Unload removes the datapath specific program aspects\n   735→func (l *loader) Unload(ep datapath.Endpoint) {\n   736→\tif ep.RequireEndpointRoute() {\n   737→\t\tif ip := ep.IPv4Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n   738→\t\t\tremoveEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip))\n   739→\t\t}\n   740→\n   741→\t\tif ip := ep.IPv6Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n   742→\t\t\tremoveEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip))\n   743→\t\t}\n   744→\t}\n   745→\n   746→\tlog := log.WithField(logfields.EndpointID, ep.StringID())\n   747→\n   748→\t// Remove legacy tc attachments.\n   749→\tlink, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(ep.InterfaceName())\n   750→\tif err == nil {\n   751→\t\tif err := removeTCFilters(link, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS); err != nil {\n   752→\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"Removing ingress filter from interface %s\", ep.InterfaceName())\n   753→\t\t}\n   754→\t\tif err := removeTCFilters(link, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS); err != nil {\n   755→\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"Removing egress filter from interface %s\", ep.InterfaceName())\n   756→\t\t}\n   757→\t}\n   758→\n   759→\t// If Cilium and the kernel support tcx to attach TC programs to the\n   760→\t// endpoint's veth device, its bpf_link object is pinned to a per-endpoint\n   761→\t// bpffs directory. When the endpoint gets deleted, we can remove the whole\n   762→\t// directory to clean up any leftover pinned links and maps.\n   763→\n   764→\t// Remove the links directory first to avoid removing program arrays before\n   765→\t// the entrypoints are detached.\n   766→\tif err := bpf.Remove(bpffsEndpointLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), ep)); err != nil {\n   767→\t\tlog.WithError(err)\n   768→\t}\n   769→\t// Finally, remove the endpoint's top-level directory.\n   770→\tif err := bpf.Remove(bpffsEndpointDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), ep)); err != nil {\n   771→\t\tlog.WithError(err)\n   772→\t}\n   773→}\n   774→\n   775→// EndpointHash hashes the specified endpoint configuration with the current\n   776→// datapath hash cache and returns the hash as string.\n   777→func (l *loader) EndpointHash(cfg datapath.EndpointConfiguration, lnCfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration) (string, error) {\n   778→\treturn l.templateCache.baseHash.hashEndpoint(l.templateCache, lnCfg, cfg)\n   779→}\n   780→\n   781→// CallsMapPath gets the BPF Calls Map for the endpoint with the specified ID.\n   782→func (l *loader) CallsMapPath(id uint16) string {\n   783→\treturn bpf.LocalMapPath(callsmap.MapName, id)\n   784→}\n   785→\n   786→// CustomCallsMapPath gets the BPF Custom Calls Map for the endpoint with the\n   787→// specified ID.\n   788→func (l *loader) CustomCallsMapPath(id uint16) string {\n   789→\treturn bpf.LocalMapPath(callsmap.CustomCallsMapName, id)\n   790→}\n   791→\n   792→// HostDatapathInitialized returns a channel which is closed when the\n   793→// host datapath has been loaded for the first time.\n   794→func (l *loader) HostDatapathInitialized() <-chan struct{} {\n   795→\treturn l.hostDpInitialized\n   796→}\n   797→\n   798→func (l *loader) WriteEndpointConfig(w io.Writer, e datapath.EndpointConfiguration, lnCfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration) error {\n   799→\treturn l.configWriter.WriteEndpointConfig(w, lnCfg, e)\n   800→}\n   801→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. masq6 netip.Addr) {\n\tif cfg.DeriveMasqIPAddrFromDevice != \"\" {\n\t\tifName = cfg.DeriveMasqIPAddrFromDevice\n\t}\n\n\tfind := func(devName string) bool {\n\t\tfor _, addr := range cfg.NodeAddresses {\n\t\t\tif addr.DeviceName != devName {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif !addr.Primary {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif addr.Addr.Is4() && !masq4.IsValid() &&\n\t\t\t\t(!option.Config.EnableIPv6Masquerade || masq6.IsValid())\n\t\t\tif done {\n\t\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// Try to find suitable masquerade address first from the given interface.\n\tif !find(ifName) {\n\t\t// No suitable masquerade addresses were found for this device. Try the fallback\n\t\t// addresses.\n\t\tfind(tables.WildcardDeviceName)\n\t}\n\n\treturn\n}\n\n// hostRewrites calculates the changes necessary to attach the host endpoint\n// programs to different interfaces.\nfunc hostRewrites(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, ifName string) (map[string]uint64, map[string]string, error) {\n\topts := ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep)\n\tstrings := ELFMapSubstitutions(ep)\n\n\tiface, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(ifName)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, err\n\t}\n\n\t// The THIS_INTERFACE_MAC value is specific to each attachment interface.\n\tmac := mac.MAC(iface.Attrs().HardwareAddr)\n\tif mac == nil {\n\t\t// L2-less device\n\t\tmac = make([]byte, 6)\n\t\topts[\"ETH_HLEN\"] = uint64(0)\n\t}\n\topts[\"THIS_INTERFACE_MAC_1\"] = uint64(sliceToBe32(mac[0:4]))\n\topts[\"THIS_INTERFACE_MAC_2\"] = uint64(sliceToBe16(mac[4:6]))\n\n\tifIndex := uint32(iface.Attrs().Index)\n\n\tif !option.Config.EnableHostLegacyRouting {\n\t\topts[\"SECCTX_FROM_IPCACHE\"] = uint64(secctxFromIpcacheEnabled)\n\t} else {\n\t\topts[\"SECCTX_FROM_IPCACHE\"] = isObsoleteDev(dev string, devices []string) bool {\n\t// exclude devices we never attach to/from_netdev to.\n\tfor _, prefix := range defaults.ExcludedDevicePrefixes {\n\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(dev, prefix) {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// exclude devices that will still be managed going forward.\n\tfor _, d := range devices {\n\t\tif dev == d {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn true\n}\n\n// removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms removes cil_to_netdev and cil_from_netdev from devices\n// that cilium potentially doesn't manage anymore after a restart, e.g. if the set of\n// devices changes between restarts.\n//\n// This code assumes that the agent was upgraded from a prior version while maintaining\n// the same list of managed physical devices. This ensures that all tc bpf filters get\n// replaced using the naming convention of the 'current' agent build. For example,\n// before 1.13, most filters were named e.g. bpf_host.o:[to-host], to be changed to\n// cilium-<device> in 1.13, then to cil_to_host-<device> in 1.14. As a result, this\n// function only cleans up filters following the current naming scheme.\nfunc removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms(devices []string) error {\n\tlinks, err := safenetlink.LinkList()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"retrieving all netlink devices: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// collect all devices that have netdev programs attached on either ingress or egress.\n\tingressDevs := []netlink.Link{}\n\tegressDevs := []netlink.Link{}\n\tfor _, l := range links {\n\t\tif !isObsoleteDev(l.Attrs().Name, devices) {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Remove the per-device bpffs directory containing pinned links and\n\t\t// per-endpoint maps.\n\t\tbpffsPath := bpffsDeviceDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), l)\n\t\tif err := bpf.Remove(bpffsPath); err != nil {\n\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).WithField(logfields.Device, l.Attrs().Name)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tingressFilters, err := safenetlink.FilterList(l, directionToParent(dirIngress))\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"listing ingress filters: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tfor _, filter := range ingressFilters {\n\t\t\tif bpfFilter, ok := filter.(*netlink.BpfFilter); ok {\n\t\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(bpfFilter.Name, symbolFromHostNetdevEp) {\n\t\t\t\t\tingressDevs = append(ingressDevs, l)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tegressFilters, err := safenetlink.FilterList(l, directionToParent(dirEgress))\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"listing egress filters: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tfor _, filter := range egressFilters {\n\t\t\tif bpfFilter, ok := filter.(*netlink.BpfFilter); ok {\n\t\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(bpfFilter.Name, symbolToHostNetdevEp) {\n\t\t\t\t\tegressDevs = append(egressDevs, l)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, dev := range ingressDevs {\n\t\terr = removeTCFilters(dev, directionToParent(dirIngress))\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"couldn't remove ingress tc filters from %s\", dev.Attrs().Name)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, dev := range egressDevs {\n\t\terr = removeTCFilters(dev, directionToParent(dirEgress))\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"couldn't remove egress tc filters from %s\", dev.Attrs().Name)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// reloadHostEndpoint (re)attaches programs from bpf_host.c to cilium_host,\n// cilium_net and external (native) devices.\nfunc reloadHostEndpoint(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n\t// Replace programs on cilium_host.\n\tif err := attachCiliumHost(ep, spec); This is done on a per endpoint-basis,\n   151→// however, and it is possible that policy update succeeds for some endpoints,\n   152→// while it fails for other endpoints.\n   153→//\n   154→// Failure may be due to any error in obtaining information for computing policy,\n   155→// or if policy could not be generated given the current set of rules in the repository.\n   156→//\n   157→// endpoint lock must NOT be held. This will be called after\n   253→\t\t// new redirects have been acknowledged, and policy maps and NetworkPolicy have been\n   254→\t\t// updated.  We are not waiting for an acknowledgement for the removal.\n   255→\t\tvar previousRedirects map[string]uint16\n   256→\t\tif e.desiredPolicy != nil {\n   257→\t\t\tpreviousRedirects = e.desiredPolicy.Redirects\n   258→\t\t}\n   259→\t\tdatapathRegenCtxt.finalizeList.Append(func() {\n   260→\t\t\t// At the point of this call, traffic is no longer redirected to the proxy\n   261→\t\t\t// for now-obsolete redirects, since we synced the updated policy map above.\n   262→\t\t\t// It's now safe to remove the redirects from the proxy's configuration.\n   263→\t\t\te.removeOldRedirects(desiredRedirects, previousRedirects)\n   264→\t\t})\n   265→\t}\n   266→\te.runlock()\n   267→\n   268→\t// DistillPolicy converts a SelectorPolicy in to an EndpointPolicy\n   269→\tresult.endpointPolicy = selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy(e, desiredRedirects)\n   270→\n   271→\tdatapathRegenCtxt.policyResult = result\n   272→\treturn nil\n   273→}\n   274→\n   275→// setDesiredPolicy updates the endpoint with the results of a policy calculation.\n   276→//\n   277→// The endpoint write lock must be held and not released until the desired policy has\n   278→// been pushed in to the policymaps via `syncPolicyMapWith`. This is so that we block\n   279→// ApplyPolicyMapChanges, which has the effect of blocking the ipcache from updating\n   280→// the ipcache bpf map. It is required that any pending changes are pushed in to\n   281→// the policymap before the ipcache map, otherwise endpoints could experience transient\n   282→// policy drops.\n   283→//\n   284→// Specifically, since policy is calculated asynchronously from the ipcacache's apply loop,\n   285→// it is probable that the new policy diverges from the bpf PolicyMap. So, we cannot safely\n   286→// consume incremental changes (and thus allow the ipcache to continue) until we have\n   287→// successfully performed a full sync with the endpoints PolicyMap. Otherwise,\n   288→// the ipcache may remove an identity from the ipcache that the bpf PolicyMap is still\n   289→// relying on.\n   290→func (e *Endpoint) setDesiredPolicy(datapathRegenCtxt *datapathRegenerationContext) error {\n   291→\tres := datapathRegenCtxt.policyResult\n   292→\t// nil result means endpoint had no identity while policy was calculated\n   293→\tif res == nil {\n   294→\t\tif e.SecurityIdentity != nil {\n   295→\t\t\te.getLogger().Info(\"Endpoint SecurityIdentity changed during policy regeneration\")\n   296→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"endpoint %d SecurityIdentity changed during policy regeneration\", e.ID)\n   297→\t\t}\n   298→\n   299→\t\treturn nil\n   300→\t}\n   301→\t// if the security identity changed, reject the policy computation\n   302→\tif e.identityRevision != res.identityRevision {\n   303→\t\t// Detach the rejected endpoint policy.\n   304→\t\t// This is needed to release resources held for the EndpointPolicy\n   305→\t\tres.release()\n   306→\n   307→\t\te.getLogger().Info(\"Endpoint SecurityIdentity changed during policy regeneration\")\n   308→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"endpoint %d SecurityIdentity changed during policy regeneration\", e.ID)\n   309→\t}\n   310→\n   311→\toldNextPolicyRevision := e.nextPolicyRevision\n   312→\t// Set the revision of this endpoint to the current revision of the policy\n   313→\t// repository.\n   314→\te.setNextPolicyRevision(res.policyRevision)\n   315→\n   316→\tif res.endpointPolicy != nil && res.endpointPolicy != e.desiredPolicy {\n   317→\t\tif e.desiredPolicy != e.realizedPolicy {\n   318→\t\t\t// Not sure if this can happen, but Detach e.desiredPolicy before we loose\n   319→\t\t\t// the only reference to it.\n   320→\n   321→\t\t\t// Mark as \"ready\" so that Detach will not complain about it\n   322→\t\t\te.desiredPolicy.Ready()\n   323→\t\t\t// Detach the EndpointPolicy from the SelectorPolicy it was instantiated from\n   324→\t\t\te.desiredPolicy.Detach()\n   325→\t\t}\n   326→\n   327→\t\te.desiredPolicy = res.endpointPolicy\n   328→\n   329→\t\t// Revert by changing back to the old realized policy in case of any error\n   330→\t\t// This is needed to be able to recover to a known good state, as\n   331→\t\t// e.realizedPolicy is set when endpoint regeneration has succeeded.\n   332→\t\tdatapathRegenCtxt.revertStack.Push(func() error {\n   333→\t\t\t// Do nothing if e.policyMap was not initialized already\n   334→\t\t\tif e.policyMap != nil && e.desiredPolicy != e.realizedPolicy {\n   335→\t\t\t\t// Revert nextPolicyRevision; otherwise,\n   336→\t\t\t\t// res.endpointPolicy will not be recalculated\n   337→\t\t\t\t// on the next regeneration attempt, and we\n   338→\t\t\t\t// won't advance to the true desired policy map\n   339→\t\t\t\t// state. See GH-38998.\n   340→\t\t\t\te.setNextPolicyRevision(oldNextPolicyRevision)\n   341→\t\t\t\te.desiredPolicy.Detach()\n   342→\t\t\t\te.desiredPolicy = e.realizedPolicy\n   343→\n   344→\t\t\t\tcurrentMap, err := e.dumpPolicyMapToMapStateMap()\n   345→\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   346→\t\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unable to dump PolicyMap when trying to revert failed endpoint regeneration: %w\", err)\n   347→\t\t\t\t}\n   348→\n   349→\t\t\t\t_, _, err = e.syncPolicyMapWith(currentMap, false)\n   350→\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   351→\t\t\t\t\te.getLogger().WithError(err).Errorf(\"failed to sync PolicyMap when reverting to last known good policy\")\n   352→\t\t\t\t}\n   353→\t\t\t}\n   354→\t\t\treturn nil\n   355→\t\t})\n   356→\t}\n   357→\tres.endpointPolicy = nil\n   358→\n   359→\treturn nil\n   360→}\n   361→\n   362→// updateAndOverrideEndpointOptions updates the boolean configuration options for the endpoint\n   363→// based off of policy configuration, daemon policy enforcement mode, and any\n   364→// configuration options provided in opts. Returns whether the options changed\n   365→// from prior endpoint configuration. Note that the policy which applies\n   366→// to the endpoint, as well as the daemon's policy enforcement, may override\n   367→// configuration changes which were made via the API that were provided in opts.\n   368→// Must be called with endpoint mutex held.\n   369→func (e *Endpoint) updateAndOverrideEndpointOptions(opts option.OptionMap) (optsChanged bool) {\n   370→\tif opts == nil {\n   371→\t\topts = make(option.OptionMap)\n   372→\t}\n   373→\n   374→\toptsChanged = e.applyOptsLocked(opts)\n   375→\treturn\n   376→}\n   377→\n   378→// Called with e.mutex UNlocked\n   379→func (e *Endpoint) regenerate(ctx *regenerationContext) (retErr error) {\n   380→\tvar revision uint64\n   381→\tvar err error\n   382→\n   383→\tctx.Stats = regenerationStatistics{}\n   384→\tstats := &ctx.Stats\n   385→\tstats.totalTime.Start()\n   386→\tdebugLogsEnabled := logging.CanLogAt(e.getLogger().Logger, logrus.DebugLevel)\n   387→\n   388→\tif debugLogsEnabled {\n   389→\t\te.getLogger().WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n   390→\t\t\tlogfields.StartTime: time.Now(),\n   391→\t\t\tlogfields.Reason:    ctx.Reason,\n   392→\t\t}).Debug(\"Regenerating endpoint\")\n   393→\t}\n   394→\n   395→\tdefer func() {\n   396→\t\t// This has to be within a func(), not deferred directly, so that the\n   397→\t\t// value of retErr is passed in from when regenerate returns.\n   398→\t\te.updateRegenerationStatistics(ctx, retErr)\n   399→\t}()\n   400→\n   401→\te.buildMutex.Lock()\n   402→\tdefer e.buildMutex.Unlock()\n   403→\n   404→\tstats.waitingForLock.Start()\n   405→\t// Check if endpoints is still alive before doing any build\n   406→\terr = e.lockAlive()\n   407→\tstats.waitingForLock.End(err == nil)\n   408→\tif err != nil {\n   409→\t\treturn err\n   410→\t}\n   411→\n   412→\t// When building the initial drop policy in waiting-for-identity state\n   413→\t// the state remains unchanged\n   414→\t//\n   415→\t// GH-5350: Remove this special case to require checking for StateWaitingForIdentity\n   416→\tif e.getState() != StateWaitingForIdentity &&\n   417→\t\t!e.BuilderSetStateLocked(StateRegenerating, \"Regenerating endpoint: \"+ctx.Reason) {\n   418→\t\tif debugLogsEnabled {\n   419→\t\t\te.getLogger().WithField(logfields.EndpointState, e.state).Debug(\"Skipping build due to invalid state\")\n   420→\t\t}\n   421→\t\te.unlock()\n   422→\n   423→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"Skipping build due to invalid state: %s\", e.state)\n   424→\t}\n   425→\n   426→\t// Bump priority if higher priority event was skipped.\n   427→\t// This must be done in the same critical section as the state transition above.\n   428→\tif e.skippedRegenerationLevel > ctx.datapathRegenerationContext.regenerationLevel {\n   429→\t\tctx.datapathRegenerationContext.regenerationLevel = e.skippedRegenerationLevel\n   430→\t}\n   431→\t// reset to the default lowest level\n   432→\te.skippedRegenerationLevel = regeneration.Invalid\n   433→\n   434→\te.unlock()\n   435→\n   436→\tstats.prepareBuild.Start()\n   437→\torigDir := e.StateDirectoryPath()\n   438→\tctx.datapathRegenerationContext.currentDir = origDir\n   439→\n   440→\t// This is the temporary directory to store the generated headers,\n   441→\t// the original existing directory is not overwritten until the\n   442→\t// entire generation process has succeeded.\n   443→\ttmpDir := e.NextDirectoryPath()\n   444→\tctx.datapathRegenerationContext.nextDir = tmpDir\n   445→\n   446→\t// Remove an eventual existing temporary directory that has been left\n   447→\t// over to make sure we can start the build from scratch\n   448→\tif err := e.removeDirectory(tmpDir); err != nil && !os.IsNotExist(err) {\n   449→\t\tstats.prepareBuild.End(false)\n   450→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unable to remove old temporary directory: %w\", err)\n   451→\t}\n   452→\n   453→\t// Create temporary endpoint directory if it does not exist yet\n   454→\tif err := os.MkdirAll(tmpDir, 0777); err != nil {\n   455→\t\tstats.prepareBuild.End(false)\n   456→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"Failed to create endpoint directory: %w\", err)\n   457→\t}\n   458→\n   459→\tstats.prepareBuild.End(true)\n   460→\n   461→\tdefer func() {\n   462→\t\tif err := e.lockAlive(); err != nil {\n   463→\t\t\tif retErr == nil {\n   464→\t\t\t\tretErr = err\n   465→\t\t\t} else {\n   466→\t\t\t\te.logDisconnectedMutexAction(err, \"after regenerate\")\n   467→\t\t\t}\n   468→\t\t\treturn\n   469→\t\t}\n   470→\n   471→\t\t// Guarntee removal of temporary directory regardless of outcome of\n   472→\t\t// build. If the build was successful, the temporary directory will\n   473→\t\t// have been moved to a new permanent location. If the build failed,\n   474→\t\t// the temporary directory will still exist and we will reomve it.\n   475→\t\te.removeDirectory(tmpDir)\n   476→\n   477→\t\t// Set to Ready, but only if no other changes are pending.\n   478→\t\t// State will remain as waiting-to-regenerate if further\n   479→\t\t// changes are needed. There should be an another regenerate\n   480→\t\t// queued for taking care of it.\n   481→\t\te.BuilderSetStateLocked(StateReady, \"Completed endpoint regeneration with no pending regeneration requests\")\n   482→\t\te.unlock()\n   483→\t}()\n   484→\n   485→\trevision, err = e.regenerateBPF(ctx)\n   486→\n   487→\t// Write full verifier log to the endpoint directory.\n   488→\tvar ve *ebpf.VerifierError\n   489→\tif errors.As(err, &ve) {\n   490→\t\tp := path.Join(tmpDir, \"verifier.log\")\n   491→\t\tf, err := os.Create(p)\n   492→\t\tif err != nil {\n   493→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"creating endpoint verifier log file: %w\", err)\n   494→\t\t}\n   495→\t\tdefer f.Close()\n   496→\t\tif _, err := fmt.Fprintf(f, \"%+v\\n\", ve); err != nil {\n   497→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"writing verifier log to endpoint directory: %w\", err)\n   498→\t\t}\n   499→\t\te.getLogger().WithFields(logrus.Fields{logfields.Path: p}).\n   500→\t\t\tInfo(\"Wrote verifier log to endpoint directory\")\n   501→\t}\n   502→\n   503→\tif err != nil {\n   504→\t\tfailDir := e.FailedDirectoryPath()\n   505→\t\tif !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n   506→\t\t\te.getLogger().WithError(err).WithFields(logrus.Fields{logfields.Path: failDir}).\n   507→\t\t\t\tInfo(\"generating BPF for endpoint failed, keeping stale directory\")\n   508→\t\t}\n   509→\n   510→\t\t// Remove an eventual existing previous failure directory\n   511→\t\te.removeDirectory(failDir)\n   512→\t\tos.Rename(tmpDir, failDir)\n   513→\t\treturn err\n   514→\t}\n   515→\n   516→\treturn e.updateRealizedState(stats, origDir, revision)\n   517→}\n   518→\n   519→// updateRealizedState sets any realized state fields within the endpoint to\n   520→// be the desired state of the endpoint. This is only called after a successful\n   521→// regeneration of the endpoint.\n   522→func (e *Endpoint) updateRealizedState(stats *regenerationStatistics, origDir string, revision uint64) error {\n   523→\t// Update desired policy for endpoint because policy has now been realized\n   524→\t// in the datapath. PolicyMap state is not updated here, because that is\n   525→\t// performed in endpoint.syncPolicyMapWith().\n   526→\tstats.waitingForLock.Start()\n   527→\terr := e.lockAlive()\n   528→\tstats.waitingForLock.End(err == nil)\n   529→\tif err != nil {\n   530→\t\treturn err\n   531→\t}\n   532→\n   533→\tdefer e.unlock()\n   534→\n   535→\t// Depending upon result of BPF regeneration (compilation executed),\n   536→\t// shift endpoint directories to match said BPF regeneration\n   537→\t// results.\n   538→\terr = e.synchronizeDirectories(origDir)\n   539→\tif err != nil {\n   540→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"error synchronizing endpoint BPF program directories: %w\", err)\n   541→\t}\n   542→\n   543→\t// Start periodic background full reconciliation of the policy map.\n   544→\t// Does nothing if it has already been started.\n   545→\tif !e.isProperty(PropertyFakeEndpoint) &&\n   546→\t\toption.Config.DatapathMode != datapathOption.DatapathModeLBOnly {\n   547→\t\te.startSyncPolicyMapController()\n   548→\t}\n   549→\n   550→\tif e.desiredPolicy != e.realizedPolicy {\n   551→\t\t// Remove references to the old policy\n   552→\t\te.realizedPolicy.Detach()\n   553→\t\t// Set realized state to desired state.\n   554→\t\te.realizedPolicy = e.desiredPolicy\n   555→\t}\n   556→\n   557→\t// Mark the endpoint to be running 562→\te.owner.RemoveRestoredDNSRules(e.ID)\n   563→\n   564→\treturn nil\n   565→}\n   566→\n   567→func (e *Endpoint) updateRegenerationStatistics(ctx *regenerationContext, err error) {\n   568→\tsuccess := err == nil\n   569→\tstats := &ctx.Stats\n   570→\n   571→\tstats.totalTime.End(success)\n   572→\tstats.success = success\n   573→\n   574→\te.mutex.RLock()\n   575→\tstats.endpointID = e.ID\n   576→\tstats.policyStatus = e.policyStatus()\n   577→\te.runlock()\n   578→\tstats.SendMetrics()\n   579→\n   580→\t// Only add fields to the scoped logger if the stat.Total()\n   589→\t\t}\n   590→\t\tfor field, stat := range stats.datapathRealization.GetMap() {\n   591→\t\t\tfields[field] = stat.Total()\n   592→\t\t}\n   593→\t\tscopedLog = scopedLog.WithFields(fields)\n   594→\t}\n   595→\n   596→\tif err != nil {\n   597→\t\tif !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n   598→\t\t\tscopedLog.WithError(err).Warn(\"Regeneration of endpoint failed\")\n   599→\t\t}\n   600→\t\te.LogStatus(BPF, Failure, \"Error regenerating endpoint: \"+err.Error())\n   601→\t\treturn\n   602→\t}\n   603→\n   604→\tscopedLog.Debug(\"Completed endpoint regeneration\")\n   605→\te.LogStatusOK(BPF, \"Successfully regenerated endpoint program (Reason: \"+ctx.Reason+\")\")\n   606→}\n   607→\n   608→// SetRegenerateStateIfAlive tries to change the state of the endpoint for pending regeneration.\n   609→// Returns 'true' if 'e.Regenerate()' should be called after releasing the endpoint lock.\n   610→// Return 'false' if returned error is non-nil.\n   611→func (e *Endpoint) SetRegenerateStateIfAlive(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) (bool, error) {\n   612→\tregen := false\n   613→\terr := e.lockAlive()\n   614→\tif err != nil {\n   615→\t\te.LogStatus(Policy, Failure, \"Error while handling policy updates for endpoint: \"+err.Error())\n   616→\t} else {\n   617→\t\tregen = e.setRegenerateStateLocked(regenMetadata)\n   618→\t\te.unlock()\n   619→\t}\n   620→\treturn regen, err\n   621→}\n   622→\n   623→// setRegenerateStateLocked tries to change the state of the endpoint for pending regeneration.\n   624→// returns 'true' if 'e.Regenerate()' should be called after releasing the endpoint lock.\n   625→func (e *Endpoint) setRegenerateStateLocked(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) bool {\n   626→\tvar regen bool\n   627→\tstate := e.getState()\n   628→\tswitch state {\n   629→\tcase StateRestoring, StateWaitingToRegenerate:\n   630→\t\t// Bump the skipped regeneration level if needed so that the existing/queued\n   631→\t\t// regeneration can regenerate on the required level.\n   632→\t\tif regenMetadata.RegenerationLevel > e.skippedRegenerationLevel {\n   633→\t\t\te.skippedRegenerationLevel = regenMetadata.RegenerationLevel\n   634→\t\t\te.logStatusLocked(Other, OK, fmt.Sprintf(\"Skipped duplicate endpoint regeneration level %s trigger due to %s\", regenMetadata.RegenerationLevel.String(), regenMetadata.Reason))\n   635→\t\t} else {\n   636→\t\t\te.logStatusLocked(Other, OK, fmt.Sprintf(\"Skipped duplicate endpoint regeneration trigger due to %s\", regenMetadata.Reason))\n   637→\t\t}\n   638→\t\tregen = false\n   639→\tdefault:\n   640→\t\tregen = e.setState(StateWaitingToRegenerate, fmt.Sprintf(\"Triggering endpoint regeneration due to %s\", regenMetadata.Reason))\n   641→\t}\n   642→\treturn regen\n   643→}\n   644→\n   645→// UpdatePolicy updates the endpoint's policy.\n   646→// If the endpoint's identity is in the set that needs regeneration, it will queue a regeneration\n   647→// and wait for the result. If not, the endpoint's policy revision will be bumped to toRev without\n   648→// a regeneration\n   649→func (e *Endpoint) UpdatePolicy(idsToRegen *set.Set[identityPkg.NumericIdentity], fromRev, toRev uint64) {\n   650→\t// no deferred unlocks here, as we must\n   651→\t// release locks before regenerating\n   652→\n   653→\te.buildMutex.Lock() // buildMutex is required to update policy revision\n   654→\tif err := e.lockAlive(); err != nil {\n   655→\t\te.buildMutex.Unlock()\n   656→\t\treturn\n   657→\t}\n   658→\n   659→\tunlock := func() {\n   660→\t\te.unlock()\n   661→\t\te.buildMutex.Unlock()\n   662→\t}\n   663→\n   664→\tsecID := e.getIdentity()\n   665→\tif secID == identityPkg.InvalidIdentity {\n   666→\t\tunlock()\n   667→\t\treturn\n   668→\t}\n   669→\n   670→\t// If this endpoint's security ID has a policy update, we must regenerate. Otherwise,\n   671→\t// bump the policy revision directly (as long as we didn't miss an update somehow).\n   672→\tif !idsToRegen.Has(secID) {\n   673→\t\tif e.policyRevision < fromRev {\n   674→\t\t\t// FIXME: https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/36493\n   675→\t\t\t// Currently policy repository version can be bumped through multiple triggers\n   676→\t\t\t// async to each other. This can lead to out of order processing of regeneration\n   677→\t\t\t// events. The channel returns:\n   704→//   - false if the regeneration failed\n   705→//   - true if the regeneration succeed\n   706→//   - nothing and the channel is closed if the regeneration did not happen\n   707→func (e *Endpoint) RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) <-chan bool {\n   708→\tregen, err := e.SetRegenerateStateIfAlive(regenMetadata)\n   709→\tif err != nil {\n   710→\t\tlog.WithError(err).Debugf(\"Endpoint disappeared while queued to be regenerated: %s\", regenMetadata.Reason)\n   711→\t}\n   712→\tif regen {\n   713→\t\t// Regenerate logs status according to the build success/failure\n   714→\t\treturn e.Regenerate(regenMetadata)\n   715→\t}\n   716→\n   717→\tch := make(chan bool)\n   718→\tclose(ch)\n   719→\treturn ch\n   720→}\n   721→\n   722→// Regenerate forces the regeneration of endpoint programs & policy\n   723→// Should only be called with e.state at StateWaitingToRegenerate,\n   724→// StateWaitingForIdentity, or StateRestoring\n   725→func (e *Endpoint) Regenerate(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) <-chan bool {\n   726→\thr := e.GetReporter(\"datapath-regenerate\")\n   727→\tdone := make(chan bool, 1)\n   728→\n   729→\tvar (\n   730→\t\tctx   context.Context\n   731→\t\tcFunc context.CancelFunc\n   732→\t)\n   733→\n   734→\tif regenMetadata.ParentContext != nil {\n   735→\t\tctx, cFunc = context.WithCancel(regenMetadata.ParentContext)\n   736→\t} else {\n   737→\t\tctx, cFunc = context.WithCancel(e.aliveCtx)\n   738→\t}\n   739→\n   740→\tregenContext := ParseExternalRegenerationMetadata(ctx, cFunc, regenMetadata)\n   741→\n   742→\tepEvent := eventqueue.NewEvent(&EndpointRegenerationEvent{\n   743→\t\tregenContext: regenContext,\n   744→\t\tep:           e,\n   745→\t})\n   746→\n   747→\t// This may block if the Endpoint's EventQueue is full. off of the\n// rules in regeneration.Owner's policy repository.\n//\n// Policy generation may fail, and in that case we exit before actually changing\n// the policy in any way, so that the last policy remains fully in effect if the\n// new policy can not be implemented. This is done on a per endpoint-basis,\n// however, and it is possible that policy update succeeds for some endpoints,\n// while it fails for other endpoints.\n//\n// Failure may be due to any error in obtaining information for computing policy,\n// or if policy could not be generated given the current set of rules in the repository.\n//\n// endpoint lock must NOT be held. This is because the ipcache needs to be able to\n// make progress while generating policy, and *that* needs the endpoint unlocked to call\n// ep.ApplyPolicyMapChanges. Specifically, computing policy may cause identity allocation\n// which requires ipcache progress.\n//\n// buildMutex MUST be held, and not released until setDesiredPolicy and\n// updateRealizedState have been called\n//\n// There are a few fields that depend on this exact configuration of locking:\n//   - ep.desiredPolicy: ep.mutex must be locked between writing this and committing to\n//     the policy maps, or else policy drops may occur\n//   - ep.policyRevision: ep.mutex and ep.buildMutex must be held to write to this\n//   - ep.selectorPolicy: this may be nulled if the endpoints identity changes; we must\n//     check for this when committing. ep.mutex must be held\n//   - ep.realizedRedirects: this is read by external callers as part of policy generation,\n//     so ep.mutex must not be required to read this. Instead, both ep.mutex and ep.buildMutex\n//     must be held to write to this (i.e. we are deep in regeneration)\n//\n// Stores the result in 'datapathRegenCtxt.policyResult' that should be passed to setDesiredPolicy\n// after the endpoint's write lock has been acquired, returns err if recomputing policy failed.\nfunc (e *Endpoint) regeneratePolicy(stats *regenerationStatistics, datapathRegenCtxt *datapathRegenerationContext) error {\n\tvar (\n\t\terr error\n\t\tff  revert.FinalizeFunc\n\t\trf  revert.RevertFunc\n\t)\n\n\t// lock the endpoint, read our values, then unlock\n\terr = e.lockAlive()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\t// No point in calculating policy if endpoint does not have an identity yet.\n\tif e.SecurityIdentity == nil {\n\t\te.getLogger().Warn(\"Endpoint lacks identity, skipping policy calculation\")\n\t\te.unlock()\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\t// Copy out some values we care about, then unlock\n\tforcePolicyCompute := e.forcePolicyCompute\n\tsecurityIdentity := e.SecurityIdentity\n\n\t// We are computing policy; set this to false.\n\t// We do this now, not in setDesiredPolicy(), because if another caller\n\t// comes in and forces computation, we should leave that for the *next*\n\t// regeneration.\n\te.forcePolicyCompute = false\n\n\tresult := &policyGenerateResult{\n\t\tendpointPolicy: We are not waiting for an acknowledgement for the removal.\n\t\tvar previousRedirects map[string]uint16\n\t\tif e.desiredPolicy != nil {\n\t\t\tpreviousRedirects = e.desiredPolicy.Redirects\n\t\t}\n\t\tdatapathRegenCtxt.finalizeList.Append(func() {\n\t\t\t// At the point of this call, traffic is no longer redirected to the proxy\n\t\t\t// for now-obsolete redirects, since we synced the updated policy map above.\n\t\t\t// It's now safe to remove the redirects from the proxy's configuration.\n\t\t\te.removeOldRedirects(desiredRedirects, previousRedirects)\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\te.runlock()\n\n\t// DistillPolicy converts a SelectorPolicy in to an EndpointPolicy\n\tresult.endpointPolicy = selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy(e, desiredRedirects)\n\n\tdatapathRegenCtxt.policyResult = result\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// setDesiredPolicy updates the endpoint with the results of a policy calculation.\n//\n// The endpoint write lock must be held and not released until the desired policy has\n// been pushed in to the policymaps via `syncPolicyMapWith`. This is so that we block\n// ApplyPolicyMapChanges, which has the effect of blocking the ipcache from updating\n// the ipcache bpf map. It is required that any pending changes are pushed in to\n// the policymap before the ipcache map, otherwise endpoints could experience transient\n// policy drops.\n//\n// Specifically, since policy is calculated asynchronously from the ipcacache's apply loop,\n// it is probable that the new policy diverges from the bpf PolicyMap. So, we cannot safely\n// consume incremental changes (and thus allow the ipcache to continue) until we have\n// successfully performed a full sync with the endpoints PolicyMap. Otherwise,\n// the ipcache may remove an identity from the ipcache that the bpf PolicyMap is still\n// relying on.\nfunc (e *Endpoint) setDesiredPolicy(datapathRegenCtxt *datapathRegenerationContext) {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_014rLRzUHLsWufwuJDS7gHA5","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01SxbCmzzRDcLHYR6J8M5c1t","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation\n\n## Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle\n\n### What component compiles eBPF programs?\n\nThe `loader` struct in `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:74` is the central component responsible for compiling, loading, and attaching eBPF programs on each node. Its `ReloadDatapath()` method (`loader.go:700`) drives the full lifecycle for a given endpoint.\n\nThe actual compiler invocation is in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go`. The `compile()` function (`compile.go:170`) forks `clang` as a subprocess, feeds it the BPF C source file, and captures the resulting ELF object. The higher-level `compileDatapath()` (`compile.go:266`) selects between endpoint and host-endpoint programs. Each program type (lxc endpoint, host endpoint, overlay, WireGuard) is compiled on-demand when needed.\n\n### How does node-specific configuration affect compilation?\n\nTwo mechanisms inject node-specific configuration:\n\n1. **Kernel ISA probing**: `getBPFCPU()` (`compile.go:135`) runs once per agent startup using `sync.Once`. It calls `probes.HaveV3ISA()` and `probes.HaveV2ISA()` to detect what BPF instruction set the local kernel supports, then passes `-mcpu=v3`, `-mcpu=v2`, or `-mcpu=v1` to `clang` (`compile.go:192`). This means a node on kernel 5.10+ gets v3 instructions while an older node gets v1.\n\n2. **LocalNodeConfiguration hashing**: The `objectCache.build()` method (`cache.go:115`) takes a `*datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration` struct containing node-specific settings (IP addresses, enabled features, device names, etc.). `WriteEndpointConfig()` (`cache.go:141`) renders this into a C header file used during compilation. `UpdateDatapathHash()` (`cache.go:58`) invalidates the template cache when node config changes. The hash is computed by `hashDatapath()` via `hashTemplate()` (`cache.go:170`).\n\n### When does the eBPF program become node-local vs. cluster-wide?\n\neBPF programs are always node-local. The eBPF ELF is compiled into a node-local directory (`option.Config.StateDir`). The program becomes \"live\" (attached) when `reloadEndpoint()` (`loader.go:511`) calls `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` to load the ELF into the kernel and then `attachSKBProgram()` to attach it to the endpoint's veth interface via TC or TCX hooks. All of this happens entirely within the local kernel — no cluster-wide coordination is needed or performed.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### How is the Cilium agent deployed?\n\nCilium is deployed as a Kubernetes **DaemonSet** (`install/kubernetes/cilium/templates/cilium-agent/daemonset.yaml:16`, `kind: DaemonSet`). The DaemonSet ensures exactly one Cilium agent pod runs on every eligible node. Each pod runs in the host network namespace (`hostNetwork: true`, line 771 of the same file) so it has direct access to the node's network interfaces.\n\n### What happens when one node's agent fails to initialize eBPF programs?\n\nWhen `regenerateBPF()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:379`) fails, the error propagates up through `realizeBPFState()` (`bpf.go:548-586`) → `regenerate()` (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:485`). The endpoint is moved to the `FailedDirectoryPath()`, the error is logged locally (`policy.go:503-513`), and the endpoint status is set to `Failure` via `LogStatus(BPF, Failure, ...)` (`policy.go:600`).\n\nCrucially, `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` (`policy.go:908`) starts a controller loop *on the same node* that retries regeneration with exponential backoff. The failure is self-contained: no signal is sent to other nodes, no cluster-wide state is altered.\n\nIf the Cilium agent pod itself crashes and restarts, the DaemonSet controller schedules a new pod on the same node. Other nodes' DaemonSet pods are independent and continue running.\n\n### How does the control plane vs. data plane split contribute to isolation?\n\nThe control plane (Kubernetes API server, CRD storage via etcd) is entirely separate from the data plane (eBPF programs attached to TC hooks). The Cilium agent is a pure consumer of control-plane policy resources. Even if the data plane fails to compile or load eBPF programs on one node, the agent on that node continues polling the Kubernetes API and maintaining its in-memory policy state. Other nodes' agents have their own independent API watches and their own compilation pipelines — they are not blocked, notified, or affected by a neighbor's BPF failure.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How are CiliumNetworkPolicy resources distributed to each node?\n\nEach Cilium agent independently watches Kubernetes CRD resources using the `policyWatcher` struct (`pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go:26`). The `watchResources()` method (`watcher.go:71`) subscribes to Kubernetes API event streams for `CiliumNetworkPolicy`, `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy`, and standard `NetworkPolicy` resources. This is a standard Kubernetes informer pattern: each agent gets its own list-watch connection to the API server. Changes are received independently on each node without routing through any other Cilium agent.\n\n### What component translates policies into eBPF bytecode?\n\nThe translation chain is:\n\n1. **`policyWatcher.onUpsert()`** (`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go:23`) receives the CRD update and calls `policyImporter.UpdatePolicy()`.\n2. **`policyImporter.processUpdates()`** (`pkg/policy/cell/policy_importer.go:263`) updates the local `policy.Repository` and calls `endpointManager.UpdatePolicy()`.\n3. **`Endpoint.UpdatePolicy()`** (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:649`) checks if the endpoint's security identity is affected and, if so, triggers `Endpoint.Regenerate()`.\n4. **`Endpoint.regeneratePolicy()`** (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:177`) calls `GetSelectorPolicy()` on the local policy repository, then `selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy()` to produce an `EndpointPolicy`.\n5. **`Endpoint.realizeBPFState()`** (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:548`) calls `loader.ReloadDatapath()` which invokes `objectCache.fetchOrCompile()` → `compileDatapath()` → `clang` to produce the final eBPF ELF and load it into the kernel.\n\n### Why doesn't a compilation failure on one node block policy distribution to other nodes?\n\nBecause the entire pipeline above executes independently inside each agent process. The Kubernetes API server simply sends the same CRD change event to every agent's informer. Each agent processes that event independently. A failure inside one agent's `realizeBPFState()` call is caught and logged within that agent's goroutine — it does not write any state back to the Kubernetes API (beyond updating the CNP `.status` field), and it does not affect any other node's `policyWatcher` or compilation pipeline.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\n### Are eBPF maps node-local or cluster-wide?\n\neBPF maps are **strictly node-local**. An eBPF map is a kernel data structure managed by the Linux kernel running on a single host. There is no mechanism for eBPF maps to span nodes.\n\n### What mechanisms ensure map isolation?\n\n**BPF filesystem (bpffs) pinning**: Cilium mounts a BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf` (the `bpffsRoot` variable in `pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:25`). `CheckOrMountFS()` (`bpffs_linux.go:295`) ensures the filesystem is mounted on each node at startup. Map pins are written under:\n\n- `TCGlobalsPath()` → `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/` for globally-shared maps (e.g., `cilium_lxc`, connection tracking maps).\n- `CiliumPath()` → `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/` for Cilium-managed maps, with per-device subdirectories (`bpffsDeviceDir()`, `paths.go:29`) and per-endpoint subdirectories (`bpffsEndpointDir()`, `paths.go:63`).\n\n**Per-endpoint policy map naming**: Policy maps are named `cilium_policy_v2_<id>` using `LocalMapName()` (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:107`), where `id` is the local endpoint ID. This is referenced in `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:88` via `bpf.LocalMapPath(policymap.MapName, e.ID)`. Endpoint IDs are local to each node.\n\n**Linux kernel namespacing**: The BPF filesystem mount at `/sys/fs/bpf` is a local kernel mount. Even if two nodes have a shared network filesystem, eBPF maps live in kernel memory and are identified by file descriptors pinned to this local filesystem. There is no cross-node sharing.\n\n### If a node fails to create or update a map, how does that affect other nodes?\n\nIt does not affect other nodes at all. When `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:345`, `515`) fails to create or pin a map, it returns an error up to `reloadEndpoint()` → `ReloadDatapath()` → `realizeBPFState()`. This error is caught locally, the endpoint regeneration fails, and `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` schedules a local retry. No cross-node RPC or state mutation occurs. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01SxbCmzzRDcLHYR6J8M5c1t","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /logs/agent/investigation.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"da22187a-8ba3-4043-a6aa-8c1f86c70ceb","uuid":"fa940eaf-95c4-4b0b-80b7-2a0e8ac71dba","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation\n\n## Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle\n\n### What component compiles eBPF programs?\n\nThe `loader` struct in `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:74` is the central component responsible for compiling, loading, and attaching eBPF programs on each node. Its `ReloadDatapath()` method (`loader.go:700`) drives the full lifecycle for a given endpoint.\n\nThe actual compiler invocation is in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go`. The `compile()` function (`compile.go:170`) forks `clang` as a subprocess, feeds it the BPF C source file, and captures the resulting ELF object. The higher-level `compileDatapath()` (`compile.go:266`) selects between endpoint and host-endpoint programs. Each program type (lxc endpoint, host endpoint, overlay, WireGuard) is compiled on-demand when needed.\n\n### How does node-specific configuration affect compilation?\n\nTwo mechanisms inject node-specific configuration:\n\n1. **Kernel ISA probing**: `getBPFCPU()` (`compile.go:135`) runs once per agent startup using `sync.Once`. It calls `probes.HaveV3ISA()` and `probes.HaveV2ISA()` to detect what BPF instruction set the local kernel supports, then passes `-mcpu=v3`, `-mcpu=v2`, or `-mcpu=v1` to `clang` (`compile.go:192`). This means a node on kernel 5.10+ gets v3 instructions while an older node gets v1.\n\n2. **LocalNodeConfiguration hashing**: The `objectCache.build()` method (`cache.go:115`) takes a `*datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration` struct containing node-specific settings (IP addresses, enabled features, device names, etc.). `WriteEndpointConfig()` (`cache.go:141`) renders this into a C header file used during compilation. `UpdateDatapathHash()` (`cache.go:58`) invalidates the template cache when node config changes. The hash is computed by `hashDatapath()` via `hashTemplate()` (`cache.go:170`).\n\n### When does the eBPF program become node-local vs. cluster-wide?\n\neBPF programs are always node-local. The eBPF ELF is compiled into a node-local directory (`option.Config.StateDir`). The program becomes \"live\" (attached) when `reloadEndpoint()` (`loader.go:511`) calls `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` to load the ELF into the kernel and then `attachSKBProgram()` to attach it to the endpoint's veth interface via TC or TCX hooks. All of this happens entirely within the local kernel — no cluster-wide coordination is needed or performed.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### How is the Cilium agent deployed?\n\nCilium is deployed as a Kubernetes **DaemonSet** (`install/kubernetes/cilium/templates/cilium-agent/daemonset.yaml:16`, `kind: DaemonSet`). The DaemonSet ensures exactly one Cilium agent pod runs on every eligible node. Each pod runs in the host network namespace (`hostNetwork: true`, line 771 of the same file) so it has direct access to the node's network interfaces.\n\n### What happens when one node's agent fails to initialize eBPF programs?\n\nWhen `regenerateBPF()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:379`) fails, the error propagates up through `realizeBPFState()` (`bpf.go:548-586`) → `regenerate()` (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:485`). The endpoint is moved to the `FailedDirectoryPath()`, the error is logged locally (`policy.go:503-513`), and the endpoint status is set to `Failure` via `LogStatus(BPF, Failure, ...)` (`policy.go:600`).\n\nCrucially, `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` (`policy.go:908`) starts a controller loop *on the same node* that retries regeneration with exponential backoff. The failure is self-contained: no signal is sent to other nodes, no cluster-wide state is altered.\n\nIf the Cilium agent pod itself crashes and restarts, the DaemonSet controller schedules a new pod on the same node. Other nodes' DaemonSet pods are independent and continue running.\n\n### How does the control plane vs. data plane split contribute to isolation?\n\nThe control plane (Kubernetes API server, CRD storage via etcd) is entirely separate from the data plane (eBPF programs attached to TC hooks). The Cilium agent is a pure consumer of control-plane policy resources. Even if the data plane fails to compile or load eBPF programs on one node, the agent on that node continues polling the Kubernetes API and maintaining its in-memory policy state. Other nodes' agents have their own independent API watches and their own compilation pipelines — they are not blocked, notified, or affected by a neighbor's BPF failure.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How are CiliumNetworkPolicy resources distributed to each node?\n\nEach Cilium agent independently watches Kubernetes CRD resources using the `policyWatcher` struct (`pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go:26`). The `watchResources()` method (`watcher.go:71`) subscribes to Kubernetes API event streams for `CiliumNetworkPolicy`, `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy`, and standard `NetworkPolicy` resources. This is a standard Kubernetes informer pattern: each agent gets its own list-watch connection to the API server. Changes are received independently on each node without routing through any other Cilium agent.\n\n### What component translates policies into eBPF bytecode?\n\nThe translation chain is:\n\n1. **`policyWatcher.onUpsert()`** (`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go:23`) receives the CRD update and calls `policyImporter.UpdatePolicy()`.\n2. **`policyImporter.processUpdates()`** (`pkg/policy/cell/policy_importer.go:263`) updates the local `policy.Repository` and calls `endpointManager.UpdatePolicy()`.\n3. **`Endpoint.UpdatePolicy()`** (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:649`) checks if the endpoint's security identity is affected and, if so, triggers `Endpoint.Regenerate()`.\n4. **`Endpoint.regeneratePolicy()`** (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:177`) calls `GetSelectorPolicy()` on the local policy repository, then `selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy()` to produce an `EndpointPolicy`.\n5. **`Endpoint.realizeBPFState()`** (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:548`) calls `loader.ReloadDatapath()` which invokes `objectCache.fetchOrCompile()` → `compileDatapath()` → `clang` to produce the final eBPF ELF and load it into the kernel.\n\n### Why doesn't a compilation failure on one node block policy distribution to other nodes?\n\nBecause the entire pipeline above executes independently inside each agent process. The Kubernetes API server simply sends the same CRD change event to every agent's informer. Each agent processes that event independently. A failure inside one agent's `realizeBPFState()` call is caught and logged within that agent's goroutine — it does not write any state back to the Kubernetes API (beyond updating the CNP `.status` field), and it does not affect any other node's `policyWatcher` or compilation pipeline.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\n### Are eBPF maps node-local or cluster-wide?\n\neBPF maps are **strictly node-local**. An eBPF map is a kernel data structure managed by the Linux kernel running on a single host. There is no mechanism for eBPF maps to span nodes.\n\n### What mechanisms ensure map isolation?\n\n**BPF filesystem (bpffs) pinning**: Cilium mounts a BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf` (the `bpffsRoot` variable in `pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:25`). `CheckOrMountFS()` (`bpffs_linux.go:295`) ensures the filesystem is mounted on each node at startup. Map pins are written under:\n\n- `TCGlobalsPath()` → `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/` for globally-shared maps (e.g., `cilium_lxc`, connection tracking maps).\n- `CiliumPath()` → `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/` for Cilium-managed maps, with per-device subdirectories (`bpffsDeviceDir()`, `paths.go:29`) and per-endpoint subdirectories (`bpffsEndpointDir()`, `paths.go:63`).\n\n**Per-endpoint policy map naming**: Policy maps are named `cilium_policy_v2_<id>` using `LocalMapName()` (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:107`), where `id` is the local endpoint ID. This is referenced in `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:88` via `bpf.LocalMapPath(policymap.MapName, e.ID)`. Endpoint IDs are local to each node.\n\n**Linux kernel namespacing**: The BPF filesystem mount at `/sys/fs/bpf` is a local kernel mount. Even if two nodes have a shared network filesystem, eBPF maps live in kernel memory and are identified by file descriptors pinned to this local filesystem. There is no cross-node sharing.\n\n### If a node fails to create or update a map, how does that affect other nodes?\n\nIt does not affect other nodes at all. When `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:345`, `515`) fails to create or pin a map, it returns an error up to `reloadEndpoint()` → `ReloadDatapath()` → `realizeBPFState()`. This error is caught locally, the endpoint regeneration fails, and `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` schedules a local retry. No cross-node RPC or state mutation occurs. Other nodes continue to create and update their own maps in their own kernel's BPF subsystem without interruption.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n| File | Relevance |\n|---|---|\n|
